        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">chicks</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer5850453">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2993356079438158257">Fannie Flagg is a brilliantly funny, authentic writer. If you ever read "Fried Green Tomatoes At the Whistle Stop Cafe" or saw the movie, you will surely like this one too.<br />It is a highly entertaining account of the formative years of a very down to eart girl growing up in Coastal Mississippi in the 50's. Great characterization! The writing style is unique and is as though Daisy were simply have a conversation with you. Most enjoyable. Give it a try!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14200702065007676618">This is one of my favorite books. It is so fun to read and fun to review. It is fun to see the adult world in this way through the eyes of an optimistic child. The story takes place during the 1950s in the South. The antics of Daisy Fay are heart-warming, crazy and at times side-splitting hilarious. I would recommend this book for everyone to enjoy.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_400093667">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400093667" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1580384-bobby" class="left imgcol" title="Bobby"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1248665099p2/1580384.jpg" alt="Bobby" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/400093667?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 25, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1580384-bobby" class="user" title="Bobby">Bobby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer400093667">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5454938728924763236">This is a coming of age tale of a young girl who dares to look at life with great optimism and sense of fun despite the fact that she is lives the unfortunate circumstance of a child with an alcoholic parent. Her father and mother's troubled marriage and her father's scheming and drinking do not dampen her zest for life, her creativity, or her spunk. Her story is shared in a diary style, yet tells far more than a diary. Daisy Fay is a maturing female who likes to write and she treasures her pape</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5454938728924763236">This is a coming of age tale of a young girl who dares to look at life with great optimism and sense of fun despite the fact that she is lives the unfortunate circumstance of a child with an alcoholic parent. Her father and mother's troubled marriage and her father's scheming and drinking do not dampen her zest for life, her creativity, or her spunk. Her story is shared in a diary style, yet tells far more than a diary. Daisy Fay is a maturing female who likes to write and she treasures her papers, ultimately keeping them in a locked box. We are privileged to read her papers.<br /><br />This is a novel that is filled with humor, yet shares life's sadness. Sometimes it is hard to enjoy the chuckle offered in Daisy Fay's life experience because of the heartache ever present. One easily comes to love Daisy Fay, who takes her circumstances as a matter of course and does not let her reality get in the way of her adventure. It is refreshing to read a story where poverty and misfortune are recognized as part of human experience, but not one that fully defines a life. <br /><br />Fannie Flagg writes a novel that clearly indicates the damaging aspects of Daisy Fay's father's alcoholism, but also presents the miracle of his imagination and spirit. Daisy provides a strong female character whose perseverance creates possibilities for a future other than what is assumed to be destiny for children who grow up in her situation. She is a self assured and self sufficient young woman who comes from a line of women who have held their own, especially her grandmothers and her great aunt. Perhaps in a small way, her mother shows strength in finally leaving her father and making a life for herself. Daisy Fay's mother seemed to have wanted more from her life and then because of her reliance on a man to take care of her, never achieved what she desired. <br /><br />I quickly fell in love with Daisy Fay when reading this novel. By the time I finished the novel, I was also in love with Fannie Flagg, her writing, her wit, her humor and her perspective on life. Fannie Flagg recognizes we all have our troubles. Some are hidden away and some are right out in public for everyone to see, but in either case we need not be ashamed by our situation. We are all worthy people and we all do better to support one another than to look down on one another. Life is to celebrate and enjoy. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5454938728924763236">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer375019139">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2534825776696196349"> It’s narrative voice is that of an eleven-year old girl from Jackson, Mississippi who is watching her parents struggle through a nasty break up and separation, her father addiction to alcohol, her mother’s inevitable abandonment of the family, and the mistakes of a myriad of other adults who should be stabilizing influences in her young life. She sees all with clarity, (perhaps only children are able to have because they are at the stage in their human development where they have no conception</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2534825776696196349"> It’s narrative voice is that of an eleven-year old girl from Jackson, Mississippi who is watching her parents struggle through a nasty break up and separation, her father addiction to alcohol, her mother’s inevitable abandonment of the family, and the mistakes of a myriad of other adults who should be stabilizing influences in her young life. She sees all with clarity, (perhaps only children are able to have because they are at the stage in their human development where they have no conception of compromise, failed expectations or the endless drive to pursue hopeless dreams) and is blindly optimistic that all will be right in her world given time. Daisy Frances Harper matures into a young woman who faces challenges around every corner. Her father’s drunken behavior, the death of her mother after an “unnatural separation” for years from her child, the bitterness of her extended family, the racist pathologies surrounding her poor white community would all pulled her down if not for her sense of loyalty, humor, and eccentric pluckiness. <br />This book was a bittersweet coming of age story of an exceptional Southern girl whose heart is as big as Alaska. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2534825776696196349">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11525038482947401306">Fannie Flagg books -the one you read when you feel that you are at your lowest point, when you feel that the world cannot get any worse, when you feel so over burdened that you are ready to go to pieces...if you can stop for a moment and pick up book, read anything written by Fannie Flagg and I PROMISE you that you will feel better...you will laugh and you will cry...you will do both at the same time...she is by far one of the best fiction/humor writers since Damon Runyon walked into Mindy's and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11525038482947401306">Fannie Flagg books -the one you read when you feel that you are at your lowest point, when you feel that the world cannot get any worse, when you feel so over burdened that you are ready to go to pieces...if you can stop for a moment and pick up book, read anything written by Fannie Flagg and I PROMISE you that you will feel better...you will laugh and you will cry...you will do both at the same time...she is by far one of the best fiction/humor writers since Damon Runyon walked into Mindy's and asked if they made more cheese cake than strudel. It is unfair to say that Fannie Flagg is strictly a Southern writer as it unfair to say that Runyon was a great New York writer...they both share an uncanny ear for the way people speak and are able to write it...you can read a Fannie Flagg novel and just walk away..her characters just stay with you and they're honest, even when they're doing something they shouldn't they remain true to themselves...<br /><br /><br /><br />I was reading this on the train one day, and burst out laughing at one point, I just couldn't stop laughing...this is a wonderful story...</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/845495-tricia" class="user" title="Tricia">Tricia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer24190850">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15299820047975748296">Daisy Fay and the Miracle Man is a coming-of-age story set in Mississippi in the 1950s. The story is told in diary entries (which I love) and follows Daisy from age 11 until after she finishes high school. Daisy is a spunky character who has to put up with a completely dysfunctional family, including an alcoholic father. There are all kinds of interesting characters involved including a crippled girl, a man with elphantiasis, an albino woman, Daisy's best friend Pickle, and Daisy's arch-nemesis,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15299820047975748296">Daisy Fay and the Miracle Man is a coming-of-age story set in Mississippi in the 1950s. The story is told in diary entries (which I love) and follows Daisy from age 11 until after she finishes high school. Daisy is a spunky character who has to put up with a completely dysfunctional family, including an alcoholic father. There are all kinds of interesting characters involved including a crippled girl, a man with elphantiasis, an albino woman, Daisy's best friend Pickle, and Daisy's arch-nemesis, Kay Bob Benson.<br /><br />Fannie Flagg manages to incorporate so many of life's complex issues into the story that it really adds depth and meaning to the experiences of the characters. The author weaves in issues such as race, abuse, and homosexuality applicable to the time period and location. <br /><br />The book is very funny, often poignant, and at times heart-breaking. But, I was rooting for Daisy the whole way and I enjoyed the journey. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15299820047975748296">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6549316306865670652">Daisy Fay Harper is now one of my favorite characters! She is spunky and independent and surrounded by a great cast of characters. This book spans Daisy Fay’s life from 1952-1959 at the beginning of the book she is 11 years old. Daisy Fay’s daddy is a drunk but she stands by him through thick and thin, he isn’t a mean drunk so that’s ok LOL.<br /><br />It is so fun to read about her discovering life especially since this book is set in the 50’s.One of my favorite scenes is when they are living in Shell Beac</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6549316306865670652">Daisy Fay Harper is now one of my favorite characters! She is spunky and independent and surrounded by a great cast of characters. This book spans Daisy Fay’s life from 1952-1959 at the beginning of the book she is 11 years old. Daisy Fay’s daddy is a drunk but she stands by him through thick and thin, he isn’t a mean drunk so that’s ok LOL.<br /><br />It is so fun to read about her discovering life especially since this book is set in the 50’s.One of my favorite scenes is when they are living in Shell Beach and Daisy likes to sneak in and watch the entertainment at the local Blue Gardenia Lounge like the one-legged tap dancer and Ray Layne the young singer but the one she is so looking forward to is a real dancer from New Orleans named Tawny the Tasseled lady and her reaction to that was “She isn’t even a real dancer!” “All she does is spin them tassels one way then the other and shake around” I laughed so hard picturing this!<br /><br />Not only is Daisy a great character but everyone else is this book is too from her bingo addicted grandma, to her daddy’s best friend Jimmy Snow who is a crop duster but seems to crash his plane a lot! Oh my I could just go on and on about this book this is the 3rd book by Fannie Flagg I’ve read and I think it is now my mission to read everything she has ever written.<br /><br />If you like southern fiction and great characters who will make you laugh out loud you must read this book!<br /><br />5 Stars<br /></span>

      <a href="/user/show/7859405-hayden" class="user" title="Hayden">Hayden</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer297781687">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer562112197268126314">I love this book. I think Fannie Flagg might just be my favorite author.<br /><br />Daisy Fay starts out as a spunky young girl with a big imagination and an uncanny ability to see the best in people. She doesn't exactly come from an All-American family, but she loves her Momma and Daddy, despite their shortcomings. Which is not to say she doesn't occasionally get into trouble, because she also has quite a knack for being mischievous too.<br /><br />What I like about this novel is that we get to see little Daisy Fay gr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText562112197268126314">I love this book. I think Fannie Flagg might just be my favorite author.<br /><br />Daisy Fay starts out as a spunky young girl with a big imagination and an uncanny ability to see the best in people. She doesn't exactly come from an All-American family, but she loves her Momma and Daddy, despite their shortcomings. Which is not to say she doesn't occasionally get into trouble, because she also has quite a knack for being mischievous too.<br /><br />What I like about this novel is that we get to see little Daisy Fay grow up. The story isn't just about one particular time in her life. It's written kind of like a journal, but with many more details than a regular diary.<br /><br />Through all her ups and downs, Daisy had people who loved her everywhere she went. And the few people that really couldn't stand her, like Roy Grimmett, Kay Bob Benson, and Claude Pistal, just couldn't understand how someone with so little could be so happy. But I understand. Daisy Fay Harper made up for what she didn't have materially with her kind heart, her faith in herself and the people she loved, and her larger than life personality. She's one of my favorite characters I've come accross in literature.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="562112197268126314">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655395021" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1618357-jay" class="left imgcol" title="Jay"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1251571565p2/1618357.jpg" alt="Jay" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/655395021?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 05, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1618357-jay" class="user" title="Jay">Jay</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6594053-daisy-fay-and-the-miracle-man" title="Library Binding 0446394452" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer655395021">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8758442079089373744">I've read almost all of Flagg's other books and saw this one on a list of best Southern books, so I had to give it a shot. If you've had kids, especially girls, in the past 10 years, you might have read some Junie B. Jones books. They are all relatively short books written in diary format told from the point of view of an elementary school-aged girl who gets herself into predicaments. Daisy Fay could well have been Junie B. with a few more years on her. While I really enjoyed reading Junie B. Jo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8758442079089373744">I've read almost all of Flagg's other books and saw this one on a list of best Southern books, so I had to give it a shot. If you've had kids, especially girls, in the past 10 years, you might have read some Junie B. Jones books. They are all relatively short books written in diary format told from the point of view of an elementary school-aged girl who gets herself into predicaments. Daisy Fay could well have been Junie B. with a few more years on her. While I really enjoyed reading Junie B. Jones books with my girls, Daisy Fay was written much more over the top. Where Junie B. would have one or two funny lines per paragraph, Flagg tried to make darn near every line funny, and I felt that was a bit too much. I enjoyed the story of Daisy Fay's life and was disappointed with where it ended, and actually, how it ended. The message to me was that the people you know, your friends, can help you along the way.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8465306335256972349">"Finora, non ho mai sentito parlare di un solo fatto della vita che mi piaccia."<br />Questo libro è il diario di una ragazzina di nome Daisy Fay Harper che vive nello stato del Mississipi intorno agli anni '50, dove il razzismo dilagava, i bianchi vivevano separati dai neri che erano costretti solo a fare lavori umili e sottomessi. <br />Con tratti ironici, taglienti e graffianti Daisy ci racconta la sua vita con un padre alcolizzato, la madre che alla fine scappa perchè non ce la fa più a stare con un uom</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8465306335256972349">"Finora, non ho mai sentito parlare di un solo fatto della vita che mi piaccia."<br />Questo libro è il diario di una ragazzina di nome Daisy Fay Harper che vive nello stato del Mississipi intorno agli anni '50, dove il razzismo dilagava, i bianchi vivevano separati dai neri che erano costretti solo a fare lavori umili e sottomessi. <br />Con tratti ironici, taglienti e graffianti Daisy ci racconta la sua vita con un padre alcolizzato, la madre che alla fine scappa perchè non ce la fa più a stare con un uomo che rovina tutto ciò che costruisce e che dopo poco tempo lascia un vuoto incolmabile nella vita della ragazza perchè muore di cancro, ha un'amica Pickle che ha un padre prete battista che la punisce spesso picchiandola, ha il migliore amico di suo padre Jimmy Snow che è compagno di bevute che si prende cura di lei e le vuole un gran bene, c'è l'eterna rivale Kay Bob Benson dove Daisy fallisce lei puntualmente eccelle e poi ci sono tanti tanti altri personaggi che costellano le sue storie quotidiane, mai ovvi, particolari, stravaganti e originali. <br />Daisy è una che non si abbatte mai, vuole un infinito bene a suo padre nonostante tutto, non si fa alcun problema e si rapporta molto anche con persone di colore, ne combina di ogni genere e mi ha fatto ridere di gran gusto la volta in cui è in riva al mare con la sua amica a prendere il sole, arriva il fratello dell'amica con un mulo e la sfida a cavalcarlo, lei accetta ci monta sopra e inizia a gironzolare con il mulo che ad un certo punto viene punto da un'ape si imbizzarrisce, lei non riesce a domarlo, il sopra del costume le si stacca e cavalca per tutto il villaggio in desabillè! <br />E' un libro ironico, semplice, divertente, ma allo stesso tempo anche toccante perchè nonostante Daisy spesso sia messa davanti al dolore, lei non si lamenta e non si arrende mai, con il sorriso sulle labbra va avanti cercando di vedere i lati positivi in quel poco che ha (è meglio mio padre che beve come una spugna, ma che non mi ha mai sfiorato, che un padre prete che ti picchia selvaggemente) e questo è il grande insegnamento che ci dà. <br />La vita ci può offrire veramente poco, ma quel poco ci deve bastare per cercare di vivere il più serenamente possibile, perchè se non accetti questo principio, puoi commettere errori e sbagli che ti faranno affrontare il tutto in modo ancora peggiore e insoddisfacente. <br />"Se la gente ti parla alle spalle, vuol dire che stai camminando due passi avanti!."</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234137587" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5189201-marlene-lewis" class="left imgcol" title="Marlene Lewis"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1301312487p2/5189201.jpg" alt="Marlene Lewis" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/234137587?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5189201-marlene-lewis" class="user" title="Marlene Lewis">Marlene Lewis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer234137587">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3788451148853300339">What a quirky tale! I must say, I wasn’t quite sure of what to make of Daisy May and the Miracle Man. In fact, I wasn’t even sure that I liked it until I found I couldn’t put it down. I love Fannie Flagg’s way of writing; she comes from left field in way, totally unpredictable and refreshingly different to most writers. She has a definite talent for capturing the eccentricities in her characters and must be a very astute observer of human nature. On the surface, Daisy May and the Miracle Man tel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3788451148853300339">What a quirky tale! I must say, I wasn’t quite sure of what to make of Daisy May and the Miracle Man. In fact, I wasn’t even sure that I liked it until I found I couldn’t put it down. I love Fannie Flagg’s way of writing; she comes from left field in way, totally unpredictable and refreshingly different to most writers. She has a definite talent for capturing the eccentricities in her characters and must be a very astute observer of human nature. On the surface, Daisy May and the Miracle Man tells a highly unlikely story about a girl growing up in the South during the 1950s. Then when you start to think about it, many of the crazy goings on could quite easily have been things that frequently did happen during those times. It was an interesting story because if it wasn’t for the humorous tack taken by Fannie Flagg, it could easily have been a very tragic story. She is a clever writer, and I don’t think anyone else could have done this story as well. My head is still struggling to put Daisy May and the Miracle Man into a category- and I am still trying to figure out who was Miracle Man! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3788451148853300339">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/10232645-katherine" class="left imgcol" title="Katherine"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Katherine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/10232645-katherine" class="user" title="Katherine">Katherine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1324556599">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14141665043032530243">If you are looking for a book the makes you laugh out loud, this is it. Daisy Fay is 11 years old at the start of the book and has just graduated high school by the end. The book is written somewhat like a diary, with Daisy telling the story as she sees it. Not surprisingly, some of her interpretations are not exactly correct, and these misconceptions lend to a lot of fun on the part of the reader. There are more serious parts to the story, but they make the funny parts even more so.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_819148120">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/819148120" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/27545392-mindy" class="left imgcol" title="Mindy"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Mindy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/819148120?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/27545392-mindy" class="user" title="Mindy">Mindy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer819148120">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7739833805383436746">I have never read a book as brilliantly funny as Daisy Faye. Whenever someone I love needs some cheering up I buy them this book and can't wait for them to read it so I can laugh with them about it. Her disarming sixth grader stream of consciousness prose was so refreshingly different from anything I have ever read. I tried to read a few of her other books and unfortunately did not find them of the same caliber… but she really hit the nail on the head with this one. Daisy Fay is irreverently, ac</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7739833805383436746">I have never read a book as brilliantly funny as Daisy Faye. Whenever someone I love needs some cheering up I buy them this book and can't wait for them to read it so I can laugh with them about it. Her disarming sixth grader stream of consciousness prose was so refreshingly different from anything I have ever read. I tried to read a few of her other books and unfortunately did not find them of the same caliber… but she really hit the nail on the head with this one. Daisy Fay is irreverently, accidentally funny in her description of her "white trash" life in her formative years. Her summers at the beach in her family malt shop, her Jr. debutante meetings and her fathers' get rich quick schemes genuinely made me laugh out loud. It's so fun and refreshing to laugh like this alongside a funny sixth grader when most comedies (and jokes for that matter) today are crude, overly sexual and lacking in imagination. Adore this book!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7739833805383436746">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1008253000">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1008253000" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/20254422-carrie-rzeppa" class="left imgcol" title="Carrie Rzeppa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1368287888p2/20254422.jpg" alt="Carrie Rzeppa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1008253000?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 27, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20254422-carrie-rzeppa" class="user" title="Carrie Rzeppa">Carrie Rzeppa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1008253000">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12788684426707906803">I think this was my favorite Fannie Flagg book, even though it is quite different than the others. The story is written as journal entries by 11-year old Daisy Fay from Mississippi, and the entries continue until she is in her late teens. The entries are Daisy Fay's stream of consciousness as she navigates through life with a drunk for a daddy, a hopelessly inept mother, and a cast of increasingly bizarre characters. Flagg's other stories portray her characters with good-natured, naive, southern</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12788684426707906803">I think this was my favorite Fannie Flagg book, even though it is quite different than the others. The story is written as journal entries by 11-year old Daisy Fay from Mississippi, and the entries continue until she is in her late teens. The entries are Daisy Fay's stream of consciousness as she navigates through life with a drunk for a daddy, a hopelessly inept mother, and a cast of increasingly bizarre characters. Flagg's other stories portray her characters with good-natured, naive, southern charm… this book has "white-trash" characters who have over-the-top experiences. Realistic fiction it is not, but I laughed out loud several times as I read from beginning to end. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12788684426707906803">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14796841">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer489260266465198783">This was funny. It got me to remember a lot of experiences I had growing up. There were parts I just laughed out loud. Others I found some language in it politically incorrect. But while reading the book you need to remember the time frame for the story is when this type of language and description of things are really different than today. Over all, I found the book a view into a life that is pretty far from my own. Detailing family deterioration, heart ache when loved ones are taken from you f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText489260266465198783">This was funny. It got me to remember a lot of experiences I had growing up. There were parts I just laughed out loud. Others I found some language in it politically incorrect. But while reading the book you need to remember the time frame for the story is when this type of language and description of things are really different than today. Over all, I found the book a view into a life that is pretty far from my own. Detailing family deterioration, heart ache when loved ones are taken from you for various reasons. How children might rationalize bad situations. It shows resiliency in tough situations coupled with some creative thinking. It will give you some laughs. </span>

        <a href="/review/show/15467709?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 13, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/742267-robin" class="user" title="Robin">Robin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody!</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15467709">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13255148008430678224">Haaaaaated it! I don't understand the inspiration behind this book (or, shall I say, the lack thereof?) For starters, what would possess a person to write a book about "white trash" in the first place? Secondly, why do her critics call it "side-splittingly funny" and "sheer, unbeatable entertainment"? I didn't miss the attempted humor...I just found this book to be morally degrading and not all that funny. Some parts caused me to wonder why on earth someone would send this book to print and not</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13255148008430678224">Haaaaaated it! I don't understand the inspiration behind this book (or, shall I say, the lack thereof?) For starters, what would possess a person to write a book about "white trash" in the first place? Secondly, why do her critics call it "side-splittingly funny" and "sheer, unbeatable entertainment"? I didn't miss the attempted humor...I just found this book to be morally degrading and not all that funny. Some parts caused me to wonder why on earth someone would send this book to print and not be embarrassed. I'm very disappointed in Fannie Flagg, as her other books I have read were great. I'm hoping this was her only exception. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer40478398">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1023616308536763797">I love this book so much--I can't tell you how many times I've read it now. It's my constant go-to recommendation book. It's a light, sweet read that's sort of like BRIDGET JONES meets YAYA SISTERHOOD. It starts in the early 1950s, in coastal Mississippi, with our heroine, 9 year-old Daisy Fay Harper. The book is written in diary form and follows her until her 17th year. She's so three dimensional and lovable, it's hard not to laugh out loud to this book. Whenever I need a palate cleanser betwee</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1023616308536763797">I love this book so much--I can't tell you how many times I've read it now. It's my constant go-to recommendation book. It's a light, sweet read that's sort of like BRIDGET JONES meets YAYA SISTERHOOD. It starts in the early 1950s, in coastal Mississippi, with our heroine, 9 year-old Daisy Fay Harper. The book is written in diary form and follows her until her 17th year. She's so three dimensional and lovable, it's hard not to laugh out loud to this book. Whenever I need a palate cleanser between books, or whenever I just can't handle a heavy read, this is where I go. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1023616308536763797">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_546255861">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546255861" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12656534-zoeytron" class="left imgcol" title="Zoeytron"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451089497p2/12656534.jpg" alt="Zoeytron" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/546255861?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 01, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12656534-zoeytron" class="user" title="Zoeytron">Zoeytron</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer546255861">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4368544016115516041">This book tickled my funny bone from beginning to end. It was full of the outrageous observations of an 11 year old girl by the name of Daisy Fay Harper. The author captured the literal mindedness of a little kid, no question about it. The setting is Shell Beach, Mississippi in the early 1950's. Residents in the small town are expertly fleshed out for us, thanks to Daisy Fay. No one escapes her hilarious notions. This one will make you smile. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer67418492">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6875141686946857236">This book was an entertaining read. It covers the whole gamut: alcoholism, disfunctional families, racisim, murder, homosexuality, you name it. Having said that, the book sounds rather lurid. It's not. It's written from the perspective of a child and done in a humorous and non-judgemental way. A good, quick read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/22576487-sydney?shelf=period-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">period-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1355842809">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3748105177882092471">I have read all of Flagg's books. Each one is heart warming and full of the pathos of everyday life. She writes of everyday people in mid 20th century America--their triumphs, heartbreaks and some of the unusual. Flagg weaves a well-written story that keeps you coming back for more.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/1084654-liisa" class="user" title="Liisa">Liisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer36947034">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2462124234000093218"><em>Fannie Flagg's<em> <strong>'Daisy Fay and the Miracle Man'</strong> has failed to ignite that Southern Charm spark which makes me usually fall in love with her books.<br /><br />Before I pass final judgement, I am going to leave it be and come back to it down the road.</em></em></span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1320832769" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4209094-pam" class="left imgcol" title="Pam"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Pam" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1320832769?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 06, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4209094-pam" class="user" title="Pam">Pam</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1320832769">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3193236954336943925">Fun book although I think I would have enjoyed an audio version better. Lots of funny, laugh out loud moments. Written as a young girl's diary beginning in 1952 and ending in 1959; lots of comments about current events, movies, movie stars, tv programs, etc. so I'm wondering if the reader isn't from somewhere around that time period, how much of some of the comments would make sense to them. I'm from that time period and some of the things she wrote about I wasn't even familiar with; that's not</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3193236954336943925">Fun book although I think I would have enjoyed an audio version better. Lots of funny, laugh out loud moments. Written as a young girl's diary beginning in 1952 and ending in 1959; lots of comments about current events, movies, movie stars, tv programs, etc. so I'm wondering if the reader isn't from somewhere around that time period, how much of some of the comments would make sense to them. I'm from that time period and some of the things she wrote about I wasn't even familiar with; that's not to say the book can't be enjoyed without always knowing what she is talking about all the time but I do think that enjoyment would be somewhat watered down.<br />As I said, there were many funny moments but it was a little over the top and a little long. Towards the end I was ready for it to be over.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3193236954336943925">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1348858508">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1348858508" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/20381969-kerrie" class="left imgcol" title="Kerrie"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Kerrie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1348858508?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 29, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20381969-kerrie" class="user" title="Kerrie">Kerrie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/199531.Daisy_Fay_and_the_Miracle_Man" title="Paperback 9780345485601" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1348858508">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16390535128210953830">I love anything by Fannie Flagg. Daisy Fay is no exception. Fanny has such a humorous style of writing but slips in a few poignant moments to keep you grounded. The book is character driven as people move in and out of Daisy's life and change her in ways she does not realize at the time. Readers watch Daisy grow up from an 11 year old through teen years, learning along with her. Daisy is optimistic despite some hard knocks that life has dealt her. The book being told by a child adds to the humor</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16390535128210953830">I love anything by Fannie Flagg. Daisy Fay is no exception. Fanny has such a humorous style of writing but slips in a few poignant moments to keep you grounded. The book is character driven as people move in and out of Daisy's life and change her in ways she does not realize at the time. Readers watch Daisy grow up from an 11 year old through teen years, learning along with her. Daisy is optimistic despite some hard knocks that life has dealt her. The book being told by a child adds to the humor and enjoyment. Daisy has a bit of information buy not the maturity to realize she only has part of the story. Her childlike (mis)understanding of the world add to the humor. The best example is when she learns that her friend was born through artificial incineration. An enjoyable, easy read that will lift your spirits and remind you to stay positive throughout life's hardships. </span>

          </span>

  }

And in this early spring of 1952, there is ample opportunity for both with sixteen-year-old and pregna&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText992298866746374131\" style=\"display:none\"&gt; The two main occupations in Limoges, Louisiana (population: 905), seem to be spreading juicy gossip and consoling the unfortunate with casseroles. And in this early spring of 1952, there is ample opportunity for both with sixteen-year-old and pregnant (by the Baptist minister) Olive Nepper, currently languishing in a coma after drinking pop laced with rose poison. But the plight of Olive and her family is hardly the only story spicing up the rumor mill in this small Southern community of unpredictable eccentrics, wandering husbands, and unsatisfied wives and few local sins will be put right by home cooking. From Michael Lee West comes a beautifully rendered portrait of small-town Southern life, filled with humanity that brilliantly weaves comedy with dark calamity. &lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a The daughter of Ringgold\'s third-generation Baptist preacher, Catherine Grace is quick-witted, more than a little stubborn, and dying to escape her small-town life. Every Saturday afternoon, she sits at the Dairy Queen, eating Dilly Bars and plotting her getaway to Atlanta. And when, with the help of a family friend, the dream becomes a reality, she immediately packs her bags, leaving her family and the boy she loves to claim the life she\'s always imagined. But before things have even begun to get off the ground in Atlanta, tragedy brings Catherine Grace back home. As a series of extraordinary events alter her perspective and sweeping changes come to Ringgold itself Catherine Grace begins to wonder if her place in the world may actually be, against all odds, right where she began. With their marriages thrown into crisis, it\'s decided that the couples absolutely must remarry on Christmas Eve. But with the church desperately in need of repairs and lacking the funds to fix the rotting floorboards and the outdated heating system, how can they ever get it ready in time?     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6125.Fannie_Flagg">About Fannie Flagg</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/6125.Fannie_Flagg"><img alt="6125" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1328803839p2/6125.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16233294948506537253"><em>Fannie Flagg</em> began writing and producing television specials at age nineteen and went on to distinguish herself as an actress and writer in television, films, and the theater.<br /><br />She is the author of the New York Times bestsellers <em>Daisy Fay and the Miracle Man</em>, <em>Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistle Stop Cafe</em> (which was produced by Universal Pictures as Fried Green Tomatoes), <em>Welcome to the World</em>, <em>Baby G</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16233294948506537253"><em>Fannie Flagg</em> began writing and producing television specials at age nineteen and went on to distinguish herself as an actress and writer in television, films, and the theater.<br /><br />She is the author of the New York Times bestsellers <em>Daisy Fay and the Miracle Man</em>, <em>Fried Green Tomatoes at the Whistle Stop Cafe</em> (which was produced by Universal Pictures as Fried Green Tomatoes), <em>Welcome to the World</em>, <em>Baby Girl!</em>, <em>Standing in the Rainbow</em>, and <em>A Redbird Christmas</em>. <br /><br />Flagg’s script for Fried Green Tomatoes was nominated for both the Academy Award and the Writers Guild of America Award and won the highly regarded Scripters Award. Flagg lives in California and in Alabama. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16233294948506537253">...more</a>

    </div>
